=300  \\$a[126] pages$b17 illustrated plates inserted
=500  \\$aThe Musikgesellschaft ‘ab dem Musiksaal’ began to publish New Year's pieces in 1685; see 04J21, 10B20, 11H13, 26D03, G1-027 and G1-028 for similar collections
=520  \\$aIn the 17th century music in Zürich was dominated by three collegia musica: the first was ‘zum Chorherrensaal’, followed by the ‘ab dem Musiksaal’ (from 1613) and ‘zur deutschen Schule’ (from 1679). Initially they were concerned only with sacred music, but later also performed contemporary German and Italian secular music. The three societies merged in 1812 to form the Allgemeine Musikgesellschaft Zürich (AMGZ), which since 1813 has produced books on musical subjects in a series of ‘Neujahrsblättern’, the successors to a series of New Year collections of polyphonic pieces published by two of the collegia musica from 1685 and 1713 respectively.

=500  \\$aJohann Anton Kobrich, the son of the organist of the 'Landsberger Stadtpfarrkirche' Maximilian Adam Kobrich († 1730), succeeded him at the age of 16 and filled this office until his death. After his wife died in 1782, he turned to theology and was ordained a priest. He wrote works for piano and organ, as well as masses, litanies and vespers. Several of his works were printed in Nuremberg and Augsburg and circulated widely in Central and Eastern Europe.

=100  1\$aClément, Charles François$d1719-1799$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q34933718$95347
=245  \\$aJournal de clavecin composé sur les ariettes de comédies, intermèdes et opéras comiques, qui ont eu le plus de succès
=260  \\$aParis$bClément$c1769
=300  \\$a72 pages
=500  \\$aCharles-François Clément (1719-1799) was a harpsichord teacher in Paris. Besides the Journal, he adapted several Italian operas for Parisian audiences, notably Niccolò Jommelli's 'L'Uccelatrice', which he renamed 'La Pipée', and Rinaldo di Capua's 'La Zingara', renamed 'La Bohémienne'. These two works were staged in 1766. Among his original works are a series of pieces for violin and harpsichord and three songs '(Le départ des guerriers' & 'Le retour des guerriers' in 1750 and 'Le Célibat' in 1762). He also wrote two theoretical books, 'Essai sur l'accompagnement du clavecin' (1758) and' Essai sur la basse fondamentale' (1762).

=500  \\$aJohn Garth (1721-1810) was an English composer, musician and teacher. Garth is chiefly remembered for his eight-volume edition with English text of The First Fifty Psalms Set to Music by Benedetto Marcello (1757–65). He also composed a set of cello concertos (op. 1, 1760) and five sets of harpsichord sonatas (opp. 2, 4–7, 1768–82), among other works.

=500  \\$aGeorge Guest (1771-1831) was an English organist and composer. He was chorister of the Chapels Royal, and may have been the "Master Guest" who was one of the principal singers (in Messiah and miscellaneous concerts) for the Hereford musical festival of 1783. Guest was organist at Eye, Suffolk, in 1787, and at St. Peter's, Wisbech, Cambridgeshire, from 1789 to 1831.

=100  \\$aBach, August Wilhelm$d1796-1869$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q71957$96950

=260  \\$aLeipzig$bBreitkopf & Härtel$c1824 [?]
=300  \\$a25 pages
=500  \\$aAugust Wilhelm Bach (1796-1869) was a German composer and organist. He is unrelated to the family of Johann Sebastian Bach. In 1816 he served as an organist at St Mary's Church and from 1820 he taught organ and music theory at the Institute of Church Music set up by Zelter. In 1832, Bach succeeded Zelter as the director of the Royal Institute of Church Music in Berlin. He also taught at the Prussian Academy of Arts. His compositions largely consist of sacred works and works for keyboard. He also wrote a pipe organ method and a hymnbook.

=500  \\$aPages 3-6 of the Kammel duets are handwritten
=500  \\$aThe duets are part of a binding with nine sets of duets for violins which once belonged, according to the inscription on the binding to "M. de Gallatin, 1er Lieutenant aux Gardes Suisses". This is Gabriel-Gaspar de Gallatin (1758-1838), a Swiss nobleman who fought in America in 1780-1781 against the British army and who later served in the Swiss Guard of Louis XVI

=260  \\$aLondon$bs.n.$c1728
=300  \\$a[vi]-12-[12]-47-[5] pages
=500  \\$aAttributed to "A. A."
=500  \\$aThis collection was dedicated to King George I and members of the royal family. Its extensive subscription list (12 pages!) is populated with a glittering array of aristocratic names, (but some scepticism has been expressed by historians of the period as to whether all those named were indeed subscribers). 
=500  \\$aContains info on tuning of the viola d'amore. The lessons for viola d’amore proved popular and were republished several times.
=500  \\$aAlthough Ariosti could sing, write drama, play the violoncello and harpsichord, his favorite instrument was the viola d'amore, for which he wrote 21 solo sonatas.
=500  \\$aContains the cantatas 'La Rosa', L'Amore onesto', 'L'Olmo', 'Libertà acquistata in amore', 'Naufragio vicino' and 'La Gelosia', for which the poetry is also separately presented in this collection (Author unknown).

=500  \\$aInteresting note concerning the role assignment printed on page 1: "le role de Babet quoique joué a Paris par une premiere chanteuse, peut être joué en province par une Dugazon, si elle est a le phisique jeune et la voix nécaissaire pour bien remplir ce rôle. l'Auteur laisse aux directeurs et aux maitres de musique à décider cette question. "(The role of Babet, although played in Paris by a female lead singer, can be played in the provinces by a female Dugazon, if she has the young physique and the necessary voice to fill the role well. The Author leaves it to the directors and masters of music to decide this question.)  A Dugazon is a singer who has a voice intermediate between soprano and mezzo-soprano, a “singing actress”, or heavier voiced soubrette. It refers to Louise-Rosalie Lefebvre (1755-1821), also known as Madame Dugazon, a famous French operatic mezzo-soprano, actress and dancer.

=100  \\$aBoni, Giuseppe Gaetano$dafter 1750-ca. 1750$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q15407614$96585
=245  \\$aDivertimenti per camera a violino, violone, cimbalo, flauto e mandola, Op. 2
=246  \1$aDivertimentio per Camera â Violino Solo è Violoncello
=260  \\$aRome$bCleton$c[1720-30?]
=300  \\$a41 pages$bengraved title page, coardboard binding, colored paper cover damaged with black ink staines, white vellum spine and corners, heart shaped manuscript title-vignet pasted on front cover$coblong
=500  \\$aBeautiful print
=500  \\$aBologna-born Pietro Gaetano Boni settled in Rome in 1711 and served as ‘cello virtuoso’ to Corelli’s patron Cardinal Pietro Ottoboni, to whom his twelve Sonate per camera a violoncello e cembalo op.1 (Rome, 1717) were dedicated. He has long been forgotten along with his compositions and technical achievements on his instrument. 
In 1717, perhaps as a result of the publication of his op.1, he was made a member of the Accademia Filarmonica, Bologna. On the title-page of his Divertimenti Op.2 he is described as a priest.
=500  \\$aDedicatee was probably Don Marino Caracciolo VI (* 22-2-1696 + 1-7-1745). The House of Caracciolo is a prominent aristocratic family originating from the ancient kingdom of Naples, the first traces of which date back to the 10th century. The Caracciolos are considered one of the most important families in the history of the Kingdom of Naples, and also held relevant posts in the Spanish Empire. 
=500  \\$a10 sonatas for the violin or traverso and basso continuo (specified on the title page: violone, harpsichord and mandola) on the cover though it says simply for violin solo and cello

=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1760. Nos.1-14 were first published in 1759 
=500  \\$aJohann Adam Hiller was a German composer, conductor and writer on music, regarded as the creator of the Singspiel, an early form of German opera. In many of these operas he collaborated with the poet Christian Felix Weiße. Furthermore, Hiller was a teacher who encouraged musical education for women. He was Kapellmeister of Abel Seyler's theatrical company, and became the first Kapellmeister of Leipzig Gewandhaus. 
=500  \\$aRegister of names of all the poets included (Christian Felix Weisse (1726-1804) , Anna Luise Karsch (1722-1791) ,  Johann Timotheus Hermes (1738-1821) , Johann Wilhelm Ludwig Gleim (1719-1803) , Müller, Johann Georg Jacobi (1740-1814) , Kretschmann, Friedrich Wilhelm Gotter (1746-1797), Johann Peter Uz (1720-1796) and Fuchs.

=500  \\$aFirst published in Cantiones sacrae (no. 33) in Antwerp,1619 
=500  \\$aThe Regina Cæli or Regina Cœli “Queen of Heaven”, is an ancient Latin Marian Hymn of the Christian Church. It is one of the four seasonal Marian antiphons of the Blessed Virgin Mary, prescribed to be sung or recited in the Liturgy of the Hours at the conclusion of the last of the hours to be prayed in common that day, typically night prayer (Compline or Vespers).   Anyone of these four or of other suitable antiphons may now be sung at any time of the liturgical year.   The Regina Coeli is sung or recited in place of the Angelus during the Easter season, from Easter Sunday until Pentecost.

=100  \\$aMouret, Jean-Joseph$d1682-1738$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q960766$96839
=245  \\$aLes Amours des Dieux. $bBallet héroïque
=260  \\$aParis$bMourette$bBoivin$bLe Clerc$c1730
=300  \\$a[ii]-3-[i]-41-47-87-75-60 pages
=500  \\$aCondensed score
=500  \\$aThe various segments are paginated separately
=505  \\$gPrologue -- Neptune et Amymone -- Jupiter et Niobé -- Apollon et Coronis -- Arianne et Bachus
=520  \\$aMouret’s Les amours des dieux is classified as a ballet-heroïque, a type of opéra-ballet that was popular during the first half of the eighteenth century. Although the term ballet-heroïque suggests the prevalence of dance, drawing on the divertissement tradition, singing and acting are also integral parts of this genre. What distinguishes the opéra-ballet from the tragedie en musique is the use of separate plots for each entrée (comparable to an act). The segments are not entirely independent, however, in that there is typically a central, overarching idea.
=534  \\$aFirst performed at the Académie Royale de Musique, Paris, 1727

=245  \\$aDie Jagd.$bEine comische Oper in drey Acten
=260  \\$aLeipzig$bBreitkopf$c1771
=300  \\$a101-[1] pages$bengraved title page
=500  \\$a'Die Jagd' is considered one of the most important early Singspiele. It was admired by Goethe and Wagner..The libretto is based on the plays La partie de chasse de Henri IV by Charles Collé, The King and the Miller of Mansfield by Robert Dodsley, and the opéra comique by Michel-Jean Sedaine (originally set by Monsigny). 
=534  \\$aThe opera was first performed at the Schlosstheater, Weimar, on 29 January 1770. 
=561  \\$aEx Libris Bibliotheca Tiliana (Plate, stamp and wax seal) = the extensive private library of the German entrepreneur, bibliophile and hunting scholar Kurt Lindner (1906-1987)

=245  \\$aLiber usualis missæ et officii pro domincis et festis cum cantu gregoriano

=300  \\$axxix-[i]-1911-12-14-12-10 pages$bloose page (manuscript)

=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aThe Liber Usualis is a book of commonly used Gregorian chants in the Catholic tradition (11th century), compiled by the monks of the Abbey of Solesmes in France. The Liber was first edited in 1896 by Solesmes Abbot Dom André Mocquereau (1849–1930). Its use has decreased since the Second Vatican Ecumenical Council (opened by Pope John XXIII in 1962), in the constitution on the liturgy (Sacrosanctum Concilium), allowed the local language to be used in Church rites.

=100  \\$aCésar, Pierre-Antoine$d17..-?1809$4arr$98211
=245  \\$aLes Varietés à la mode :$b17e Suite d'Airs, Ariettes d'Opéra et Opéra comiques, Ariettes italiennes, Romances, Vaudevilles et Duo Arrangés Pour le Clavecin ou le Forte-Piano
=260  \\$aParis$bBoyer$bLe Menu$c1785
=300  \\$a14 pages$bleather back and corners, green paper covers
=500  \\$a"Ces exemples prouvent à quelle fréquence parurent dans les périodiques, à partir des années 1760, des annonces qui proposaient des recueils d’ouvertures, airs et ariettes d’opéras et opéras-comiques, d’airs variés et de pots-pourris destinés aux différents instruments. Il s’agissait de séduire un large public d’amateurs qui aimait à se remémorer des airs connus, en lui offrant une sélection d’œuvres nouvelles et variées, mais faciles à exécuter, et d’instaurer avec lui une forme particulière de convivialité. En témoigne plus d’un titre alléchant, comme Les Variétés à la mode de Pierre-Antoine César, parues de 1783 à 1786, qui réunissaient vingt-quatre suites d’airs arrangés pour clavecin ou piano-forte. Ces transcriptions ne procuraient pas seulement, chez soi ou au concert, le plaisir de la réminiscence. Elles entendaient former le goût de l’amateur et relevaient vraisemblablement d’un système pédagogique pratiqué par les maîtres de musique, qui consistait à arranger une œuvre à l’intention de leurs élèves : ainsi le laissent supposer les nombreuses dédicaces adressées, pendant le règne de Louis XVI, à des membres de la noblesse, à l’instar du 1er Pot pouri [sic] Pour le Clavecin ou Forte Piano que Neveu dédia en 1782 à Mademoiselle de Saint-Cyr, dont il était le professeur."
from Michèle Garnier-Butel, 'Du répertoire vocal à la musique instrumentale : les transcriptions d’airs connus en France dans la seconde moitié du xviiie siècle' in Jean Quéniart, 'Le chant, acteur de l'histoire'.
https://books.openedition.org/pur/48019?lang=en

=100  \\$aAdam, Adolphe$d1803-1856$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q189544$96451
=245  \\$aDeux quadrilles, sur les motifs du Postillon de Lonjumeau d'Adolphe Adam par Julien pour piano$bavec Acc. de Violon, Flûte, Flageolet ou Cornet à Piston, ad. Lib: par Marmontel
=260  \\$aParis$bDelahante$c1836 or later
=300  \\$a5-2-2-2-2 pages$bengraved title page, editor's stamp at foot of title page, bound in carboard marbled cover, linen spine and corners, oval ms vignet on front cover$coblong
=500  \\$aParts for keyboard and various other instruments
=500  \\$aAlthough the title mentions 2 quadrilles, the score contains only one ('1er Quadrille par L. Julien') consisting of 5 parts: Pantalon, Été, Poule, Pastourelle and Finale.
=500  \\$aengraved title page by and after A. Vialon
=500  \\$aPlate nr 1304 (1)
=500  \\$aLe postillon de Lonjumeau (The postman of Lonjumeau) is an opéra-comique in three acts by Adolphe Adam to a French libretto by Adolphe de Leuven and Léon Lévy Brunswick, and premiered by the Opéra-Comique at the Salle de la Bourse in Paris on 13 October 1836. The opera has become the most successful of Adam's works, and the one by which (apart from his ballet Giselle and his Christmas carol Cantique de Noël) he is best known outside his native France. The opera is known for the difficult aria "Mes amis, écoutez l'histoire" which has been called a test for tenors because of the demanding high D, or D5, at the end of the aria. 
=500  \\$aJulien, musical conductor, the son of a military bandsman, was born on 23 April 1812 at Sisteron in the Basses-Alpes. He was brought up in barracks, was instructed in music by his father, and was admitted to the band as piccolo-player. From 1833 to 1836 he was a pupil of Lecarpentier and Halévy at the Paris Conservatoire, but instead of applying himself to serious study occupied himself with composing dance music. In 1836 he persuaded the manager of the Jardin Turc to allow him to direct some concerts of dance music. His skill as an advertiser combined with the quality of his music to attract large and fashionable crowds. His adaptation as quadrilles of Meyerbeer's ‘Huguenots,’ then new and very popular, was heralded in bombastic paragraphs, and was especially successful. Soon he was known in Paris as the Napoleon of music.

F. E. F. E. Auber, 2me quadrille et galop'

=500  \\$aJohann Gottlieb Naumann worked in Dresden, Copenhagen and Stockholm. In Sweden he assisted Kind Gustav III with his opera plans. Naumann composed over 20 operas.

Carl Ernst Naumann (15 August 1832 – 15 December 1910) was a German organist, composer, conductor, editor, arranger and musicologist. He is best known now as an arranger and editor of the music of J.S. Bach, Mozart and Mendelssohn. He was a grandson of Johann Gottlieb Naumann.

=260  \\$aDublin$bHime$c17xx
=300  \\$a[216 pages], verso pages often blank
=500  \\$aCharles Dibdin (1745-1814) was an English composer, musician, dramatist, novelist, singer and actor. He commenced a new kind of one-man-show, musical variety entertainments, in which he appeared in his own person on the stage seated at a harpsichord and played the accompaniments to his own songs, without attempting any theatrical personification of his characters.
=500  \\$aThis collection contains 89 songs, mostly on the theme of the sea, many originating from Dibdin's own dramatic entertainments.
=500  \\$aMany songs are scored for one or two transverse flutes or guitar ad libitum.

=245  \\$aMengelzangen eerste en twéde deel
=250  \\$a2nd ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bKunstgenootschap; van de Gaete; Bosch$c1717
=300  \\$a[iv]-256-[7] pages
=336  \\$anotated music
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$athis is the first edition containing the second part
=500  \\$aAndries Pels was the co-founder, with Lodewijk Meyer, of the society Nil Volentibus Arduum (1669), which is mentioned in manuscript on the spine
=500  \\$aluxurious print with a beautiful, pastoral title-page, see preface: "Wy hebben u van tydt tót tydt médegedeeld alle de stukken door het Kunstgenootschap Nil Volentibus Arduum uitgegeeven, en geene moeite, vlyt, nóch kósten gespaard, om die Dichtwérken glans en luister by te zétten, zo door het versiere van ieder stuk met een zinlyke Tytelprent, ontworpen en gesneeden door kunstryke Meesters, als ook om het wérk zelve te doen verschynen, op zeer fraai papier met nétte druklétteren, indiervoegen dat niemand met récht ons iets béters zou kunnen afvórderen. =500  \\$aThe Music for the Royal Fireworks is a suite in D major (originally for wind instruments) composed by George Frideric Handel in 1749 under contract of George II of Great Britain for the fireworks in London's Green Park on 27 April 1749. The music celebrates the end of the War of the Austrian Succession and the signing of the Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle (Aachen) in 1748.

=100  \\$aHüllmandel, Nicolas-Joseph$d1756-1823$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q588375$97650
=245  \\$aSix divertissements ou IIe suite de petits airs pour le pianoforte ou le clavecin op.7
=260  \\$aParis$bs.n.$c1783
=300  \\$a25 pages
=500  \\$aautograph signature
=500  \\$aBorn into a family of musicians, Hüllmandel began his musical studies with either Joseph Garnier or Franz Xaver Richter, or both of them, choirmasters at Strasbourg Cathedral. This is all that is known about his musical education. Fétis mentions that Hüllmandel studied with Carl Philipp Emanuel Bach, but this remains to be proven. Around the age of 20, Hüllmandel moved to Paris, where he met with immediate success in aristocratic circles and private salons, as the dedicatees of his first opuses attest: Marie-Antoinette, the Baroness Talleyrand and the Duc de Guines. He taught George Onslow and Hyacinthe Jadin. During the Revolution he moved to London, where he lived until his death. Hüllmandel composed 12 opus numbers, all for solo keyboard (harpsichord or fortepiano) or with ad libitum or obbligato accompaniment; these works were all published in Paris between 1773 and 1788, except for the last one, published in London in 1796. One wonders why he apparently stopped composing after this date. Hüllmandel also wrote the articles 'harpsichord' and 'fortepiano' for the Encyclopédie méthodique.

=500  \\$aThe Songbook is preceded by a lengthy essay (84 pages) on musical theory 'The first Principles of Music' by William Grier.
=500  \\$aQuite some songs are by Robert Burns (1759–1796) generally considered the national poet of Scotland, not only for his poems but for his songs. He avidly collected traditional melodies and composed lyrics to them if these did not exist; if they did exist, he passionately fought to preserve them in their original Scots form rather than Anglicize them.

=246  \1$aGoëss Vogl Tablature Manuscript
=260  \\$aGermany [?]$c1686
=300  \\$a66 pages$b85 blank pages, gilt edges, leather binding, embossed spine$coblong
=500  \\$aGuitar tablature with dance music. As Nigel North informed us, the first twenty and last nineteen pages of music are conceived for a five-course guitar. Twenty-six intermediary pages are dedicated to an 11-course lute
=500  \\$aMss contains 47 solos for five-course guitar tuned a d b e' and 28 solos for eleven-course lute in D-minor tuning.
=500  \\$aThe family of Sinzendorf (also: Sinzendorff) was a Bavarian-Austrian noble family
=500  \\$aThis is one of the music manuscripts from the family library of count Leopold Goëss. Most of them were kept at the family home in Ebenthal Castle in Carinthia (Austria), this manuscript belonged at least until 1997 to the library of the Landesmuseum Klagenfurt.

=590  \\$aIn welchem nicht allein die hundert und funffzig Psalmen Davids, sondern auch beyder Evangelischen Kirchen-Gesänge, mit vielen Abweichungen, nebst des Neanders Bundes-Liedern, unter welchen diejenige so bißhero nach keinen bekandten Melodien gesungen worden, in fügliche Melodien gesetzt, und insgesamt auf das Clavier mit einem richtigen Baß und sehr starckem Register aufs neue versehen. Mit vielen Melodien vermehrt und heraus gegeben...

=245  \\$aThe Complete Organists Pocket Companion$bContaining a choice Collection of Psalm-Tunes with their Givings-Out, and Interludes

=500  \\$aA blind 18th century musician based in London, Starling Goodwin wrote music both for church use and public concerts. Surviving examples of his work include voluntaries for organ or harpsichord and a number of popular light entertainment songs. One of the greatest pluralists of his profession, he was organist at four London churches simultaneously at the time of his death. He was also a witty and amusing socialiser and an accomplished violinist.

=041  \\$adut$alat
=041  \\$alat
=059  \\$av
=245  \\$aMissen en gezangen
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aUtrecht$bWeyde, van der$c1745
=300  \\$a[i]-48-[2] pages
=336  \\$anotated music
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aThe so-called 'Stukjesboek', which formed the basis of the old Catholic church song in the Netherlands: 98 songs in Latin and Dutch, plus three ordinaria in Latin. Strong Jansenist influence.
=500  \\$aMissen en Gezangen is not the only para-liturgical hymnbook that the Utrecht Church had after the schism of 1723.
Some of the material it contains had already been published in Het Paradijs, which appeared in eight editions between 1621 and 1679 in Antwerp, or in Het Prieel, Brugues 1609/l0. Also the collection of Gulielmus de Swaen, parish priest in Gouda, to which he gave the name Den Singende Swaen'[, -an allusion to his own name, which means 'swan', - contains pieces that can be found in Missen en Gezangen. Of a substantial part, however, the origin remains obscure. No doubt a large repertoire of Latin and Dutch hymns was known from the rather isolated milieu of the Utrecht church. It is even possible that the type of hymns found in Missen en Gezangen and the other collections mentioned, were cherished by the secular clergy and that their use was discouraged, more or less, by the regulars. It is at least curious that in the Old Catholic Church an abundance of hymns have survived, while they are relatively rare in the Roman Catholic Church parishes in Friesland and northern Holland.
=500  \\$aIn Missen en Gezangen we find texts by Andreas van der Schuur and Jean Baptiste Stalpaert van der Wielen , but most of the texts are from the Counter-Reformation period and are anonymous.
=500  \\$aAndreas van der Schuur (also Van der Schuer) (1656- 1719) was ordained a priest in 1680 and became parish priest in Vianen in 1692. Archbishop Van Neercassel entrusted him with the translation of the Bible  in 1732, completed by H. van Rhijn. He was the composer of several religious poems, both Latin and Dutch.


=500  \\$aJean Baptiste Stalpa(e)rt van der Wiele(n) (1579 - 1630), a lawyer in The Hague in 1598,  became a priest in 1606. In 1613 he was appointed parish priest in Delft, where he remained until his death. In 1621 he published "Hemelrijk", in 1622 "Het vrouwelick cieraed van St Agnes", religious poetry. In prose he published "Roomsche Reys" in 1624, and in 1628 a collection of hymns "'t
Gulden Jaer ons'Heeren Jesu Christi". As a posthumous work he published "Extractum Catholicum" and "Guide Jaers Feestdaghen of de Schat der gheestelijekeLofsanghen", in 1631 and 1634. He was the composer of about 2000 hymns.

=520  \\$aThe Battle of Marengo saw the French army commanded by General Bonaparte, then First Consul, clash with the Austrian army led by Field Marshal Baron von Melas at Marengo, near Alexandria in Piedmont (now in Italy), on 14 June 1800. The battle ended in victory for France.

=500  \\$aGuillo 2003 n° 1650-D; RISM L 350
=500  \\$aLa Marre, whose first name is unknown, was active as a French composer, instrumentalist and dancer in the second third of the 17th century. He is known to have contributed to, among others, the 'Ballet royal de la nuit' (1653), 'Les noces de Thétis et Pélée' (1654), 'Le Ballet d'Alcidiane' (1658), 'Hercule amoureux' (1662), and 'Le Ballet des Muses' (1666).
=500  \\$aDedicated to Henri Prévost, "maître à danser du roi", dancing master of the french king Louis XIV until 1652.
Prévost was amongst the most prominent dancing masters in the kingdom, and one of the 13 first  « académistes » who in 1661 established Académie royale de danse.

=501  \\$aBound in with 'Les Chansons pour danser et pour boire Du Sieur De La Marre', 'XVI. livre des chansons pour danser et pour boire', 'XVII. livre des chansons pour danser et pour boire', 'Les Chansons pour danser et pour boire Du Sieur Guyot', and 'V. livre des chansons du Sieur de Chancy, maistre de la musique de la chambre du Roy'

=520  \\$aFrançois de Chancy (1600–1656) was a French singer, lutenist, and composer. He was a master of music for Cardinal Richelieu in 1631, master of chamber music (1635) and was chamber musician of the Chapelle royale (1649). François de Chancy was highly regarded by Mersenne, who included Chancy's pieces in his treatises.

=100  \\$aCalvin, Jean$d1509-1564$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q37577$95913
=245  \\$aLes Pseaumes de David$bmise en rime Françoise
=260  \\$aParis$aCharenton$bCellier$c1675
=300  \\$a[626]-8-[4] pages$bembossed leather cover, front- and backmatter contains manuscript notes in French and cyphers$epostcard 
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1551, the translations of 150 Psalms of David by Clement Marot (1496-1544) as completed by Theodore de Bèze (1519-1605, Calvin's successor as spiritual leader of the Republic of Geneva) were used almost exclusively by the Calvinists (Genevan Psalter). The psalter was the main medium of popular fervour among the Reformed. The Edict of Nantes forbade Reformed worship in towns where the King of France resided and the only town allowed around Paris was Charenton. 
=500  \\$aFollowed by The Form of Ecclesiastical Prayers, The Form of Administering Baptism, The Manner of Celebrating Holy Communion, The Catechism, and Daily Exercise of the Christian. 
=504  \\$ahttps://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genevan_Psalter

=100  \\$aVoormolen, Alexander$d1895-1980$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2281256$96188
=245  \\$aCecilia (Oud Nederlandsch)
=246  \1$aCecilia. Middeleeuwsch Lied
=260  \\$aNetherlands$c1922
=300  \\$a5 pages
=500  \\$aPrinted and manuscript (Autograph?) version of the same song
=500  \\$aperformer's notes and markings in pensil on the manuscript version
=500  \\$acomposition place and date marked on manuscript version "'s-Gravenhage 1922"
=500  \\$aThis love song "Ik zag Cecilia komen" about the shepherds Cecilia and Floriaan, dates back to the 17th century. The oldest entry is in the Album of Geesken ter Borch (1652), with the opening line "Siet het pluijm gevogelt". The famous line with Cecilia is only found in verse 2 of the 2nd strophe. It also appears as "Lied van Cecilia" in the 'Dordrecht Helikon, ofte De Groote Dubbele Hollandsche Nachtegael' (1719). The song has lived on in the oral tradition, perhaps partly due to the fact that it has been included in numerous collections of folk songs. The melody is vaguely found in the Ballo di Mantova (Dance from Mantua) attributed to the guitar virtuoso Francisco Corbetta (1615-1681) and in "Fuggi fuggi da questo cielo" by Giuseppino Cenci (Giuseppino di Roma).

=100  \\$aBraunschweig-Lüneburg, Sophie Elisabeth von$d1613-1676$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q448131$98975

=300  \\$a[xxx]-265-[5] pages
=500  \\$aHyms and devotional arias
=500  \\$aSophie Elisabeth von Braunschweig-Lüneburg was a German poet, composer and impressario, and by marriage Duchess of Brunswick-Lüneburg. Most of Elisabeth Sophie 's compositions are hymns or devotional arias. Some of these were published in 1651 and 1667. The one printed in 1651, Vinetum evangelicum, Evangelischer Weinberg, is believed to have been the first music published by a woman in Germany. Her stephson Anton Ulrich was a patron of the arts, a writer, an art collector and one of the main proponents of enlightened absolutism among the Brunswick dukes.
